RATING: 7
I might be a bit partial to the theme - I love penguins - but this game turned out to be a very nice filler. Really easy to learn, plays fast and it can become quite evil (in a good way, of course). It's more about trapping your opponents and keep the most of the board for yourself than just accumulate more fish, and in its simplicity this game is more subtle than you would think at first. Compared to the game itself the setup takes time, but it’s really nothing to worry about (just prepare the board all together).
Oh, and the official "Pushing Penguins" variant is a must.

Phalanx Games version, good components.

RATING: 7
Fun little game that plays quickly. Players move their penguins to different tiles while only moving along a straight line. When you move off a tile, you pick up the tile and get points for however many fish are on it. When players can no longer move, the game is over and the person with the most points wins.

Plays great with 3. With four there is a lot less strategy but it is still fun.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
[I]tl;dr - Hey! That's my Fish is a filler classic that's dead simple to explain, but maybe more fiddly to set up than it's worth.[/I]
[COLOR=#CCCCFF]____________________________[/COLOR]

Players move penguins around and pick up the tiles that their penguins leave behind. Every tile has one, two, or three fish on it. At the end, total up the tiles you have collected and the most points wins. 

This is a quick game that's about strategically blocking other players and trying to get as many three-fish tiles as you can. As you pick up tiles the map quickly gets holes in it, and it becomes easier to block others from encroaching on fish that you want. 

I find this a solid game, but it's a little too random with more players -- I find it a better two-player experience. Also, the setup takes as long as the gameplay -- [thing=169654][/thing] is a much better filler game that's quicker to set up and just as easy to explain.

RATING: 7.5
Man, I like this game! The single and only downside to it is the set up, but I'm getting pretty fast at that now. The single largest bonus is the speed. It plays incredibly fast (in maybe 15 min) and has this simple, 30-seconds to explain, rules system that gives a very nice abstract-type strategy - except it covers what might be otherwise bland with a sassy, shiny theme of penguins sliding around on ice. Perfect!

As a side note, the fancy penguins in the deluxe version are well worth it!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
2016/01
Hey, That's My Fish is a really neat game. You have to appreciate the amount tensions and agonizing decisions that have been packed into a game that plays in 10-15 minutes. Every turn you're have to value different trade-offs while worrying about not being shut out by other players or not painting yourself into a corner, unless that secures you the whole corner. This is really the meat of the game. Another good thing is that usually when one player finds himself in a situation in which there is simply nothing more to do, the game is already very close to the end. 

I like the balance between the need to rush vs. playing safe. Moreover, it is amazing how in a game that is so fast and tactical, you can even try to execute some longer term strategies. Plays well with children as well.

However, after several plays the game can get a bit repetitive, i.e., it is always the same kind of situations you face. But I do not mind, since the game plays so fast.

RATING: 8
Smashing game to play with kids from about aged 4.  They'll love it and so will you.  It's got easy rules, but there's a fair bit of simple strategy in it and it's cute to look at.  You can really think hard about what you're going to do, but it's better to play fairly quickly, of course.  And it's easy to do variations by playing KO - 4 players start and the weakest drops out each round until there's 2, or by varying the initial tile set up.  I reckon it would work great if you made extra tiles, too, and you could even have a few different fish values in there - lots of scope if you want it...BUT this game works brilliantly as it IS.

What a little gem of a game.  Plays in about 5-10 minutes and is extremely easy to teach.  It is deceptively strategic despite its cutesy theme of penguins.  I have been playing it about 5 times a week and often play it on my phone as well.

The only reason I am not giving it a 10 is that I dislike playing it with 4 players.  I think it is the best at 3 players.  It is a great introduction abstract game that I throw on the table with people who have played chess or checkers.

RATING: 7.5
Super simple, super strategic! Like many abstract games, it's very easy to make a mistake and be unable to recover from it; however, the game is over so quickly that you don't really have much time to mope about the agony of defeat. Two annoying things about this game: it takes about as long to set up as it does to play (which isn't much time, in either case), and it's quite easy for butter-fingered players to knock the flimsy ice floes out of position.

RATING: 7
Great game. Although the set-up is a bit annoying, the game plays fast and has interesting decisions. Very easy and simple game to play - you try to get to the best spots (more fish) before your opponents do, and trying not to get blocked by the other players, unless of course you become blocked in a favorable position. Works well with 2 players, but maybe with 3 is better. With 4 players it's very messy but good anyway. A good game for non-gamers perhaps.
The deluxe version features nice plastic 3d penguin pieces, and bigger tiles.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
A cracking game for players across the entire spectrum, from children and families to gamers with an appetite for superb fillers, with the side note that it only is fun if all players are of similar capability. But when they are, it can be a brilliant exercise in optimal positioning and blocking on a rapidly shrinking bit of ice.

And I'm a sucker for flippers, it's hideously cute. The 2(?) rules take less time to explain that it takes to read this sentence, but what you are faced with is one clever hexagonal puzzle-in-reverse, in which scoring tiles are removed one-by-one. It screams out for a bigger board and special tiles, but what you get instead is probably just right. Dead-simple, dead-fast, and dead-addictive.

It is true that if one player lets something slip on their turn, someone else is likely to profit disproportionately, often giving them an advantage that can be impossible to counter. Especially in the middle game, when the ice chucks that a single player can pick unchallenged are starting to emerge. And even though not decisive, like in Settlers, well-chosen starting locations will make your food fight that much easier.

In a 4 player game you do rely on other players making the most of their options, to keep everyone working equally hard for their fish. Being the last player with 4 could also mean that all your viable options have been ripped away from the 2 penguins you have on the ice. It is often someone's weakest move that decides who the winner is, regardless. I like it better as 2 and 3 player game, as that is far less of a factor. With 2 it can be a great clash of minds. With 3 it has some sweet unpredictability. On ice that only seems appropriate.

It reminded me of Fossil on ice, but with hexagonal movement, and that is so much more interesting. Scoring is brought back to a bare minimum, and for once, stripping off complex layers and going for a the bare essentials turns this Arctic land grab into one hot experience. Recommended.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
SimpleAbstract, MultiOnly

I own the first, entirely wooden edition, called Pingvinas.  The penguin pawns in the new version look much better, but you can't beat the tiles of the old version.

The game is a very short abstract based on breaking up the board and isolating your opponents in disadvantaged positions (e.g., where they can only rake up measly amounts of fish).  It's fast, tactical, and involves penguins; what else is needed?  :)

I got the second edition in trade.  The tiles aren't wood, but they are much more practical.

RATING: 7
Good filler. Easy to learn. Difficult to master.

My latest strategy revolves around trying to move my penguins into spaces near center-placed opponent penguins in order to block them from the outlying large fields of fish. In doing so, this puts a field of fish between me and the edge of the board and it puts me between the opponent and the field of fish. So opponent in the center, then me, then field of fish, then game's edge. This strategy does not yet account for non-center placed opponents or edge dwelling oppponents. My guess would be to still apply the largest field strategy only without the limiter of the game's edge, perhaps another opponents  piece, or my own. Hmmm.

RATING: 8
A deceptively great game.  Easy to learn but contains strategy to satisfy gamers.  My kids have devised a couple of variants for Hey! That's My Fish!.
#1 - Floating - If your penguin becomes isolated, you can spend one turn to float him back to the nearest section of the board.  He may move normally on the next turn.
#2 - Fish Hunter - Start by setting up the board with the tiles upside down.  Play as usual.  It is a surprise to find out what your tile holds.
#3 - Holes - turn some of the tiles upside down in a regular game to create holes in the ice. Your penguins can jump in one hole to emerge through another on another part of the board. 
#4 - Bump! - Another version of this lets you spend your turn to bump another penguin into a hole thereby costing him a turn to get out.  Beware!
I hope these help make an already fun game even more fun.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Cambiado a Waltien en la BSK por un Warhammer invasión (junto a un Atlanteon y un Hive), en Octubre de 2010

Juego hipersencillo. Cada jugador parte con una serie de pinguinos que se mueven sobre unas losetas hexagonales, siempre en linea recta, y no pudiendo saltar huecos vacíos ni a otros pinguinos. Cuando un pinguino se mueve, el jugador se queda la loseta de la que partió su movimiento. Las losetas contienen 1, 2 o 3 peces. La partida finaliza cuando nadie se puede seguir moviendo. El que más peces haya pescado, gana. 

Se explica en un minuto y se juega en 10 o 15. Se tarda casi más en montar el tablero. Es un juego indicado para no jugones, o para rellenar huecos en sesiones jugonas. Tiene un toquecito de estrategia, pero sin complicaciones.

Prestado a Jose el Cantabro el 15/4/2011
Vendido a Jose el Cantabro el 13/5/2011 por 15€

RATING: 8
Phalanx' many travails left me completely unprepared for this wonderful little gem of a game. Fast-playing, simple, fun, and interesting, this is a great opener and or closer and is surprisingly thoughtful for a little game. The theme is wonderful, and the Phalanx production is great. When it comes to light games, give me something simple, clever, and artful like this over the more pondorous Ticket to Ride (the game we played before H!TMF!) any day.

This was a surprise winner, and I'm sorry I missed playing it last year when it came out in English, because it would have comfortably made my "best of 2005" list.

UPDATE: The replaybility of this hasn't been quite what I hoped. After about 20 games, it's lost its edge for me. But still, 20 games for a game at this level is excellent.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
It's clever, quick, and quite interactive. On your turn you will want to move all of your penguins, but you can't. So it's certainly got tension as well.

To note, the game is vicious. It is not about collecting fishes, it is about cornering the other penguins so that that they can't get any.

A design feature I really appreciate is that, compared to a game like Amazons (a very similar game), the beginning is more interesting. At the beginning of Amazons, there is no real reason to do anything. You make moves because it is your turn, the game is far too opaque at that stage to evaluate what is a good move and what isn't (at higher levels this may not be true, but at my level it is and it turns me off enough such that I won't be getting any better). However, in HTMF, you know what a good move early on is, it's a move that gets you three points as opposed to one or two. Now, eventually the game is about claiming area for yourself, and it's important to know when to transition, but early on the moves are not opaque because there is a secondary objective, get short term points.

The games biggest flaw is likely that the set-up time is equal to the play time. However, if played on a tablet, the game is awesome and would be rated much higher.

Unfortunately for HTMF, Battle Sheep has a very similar feel in play, but is much faster to setup.

2013/08/16: Ouch,my brain hurts after playing this game. I won the first game my group played, but it was beginners luck. Never won since! Oh well, I guess I'm not that smart...
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is really a perfect little abstract. It's not the brain burner many classic abstracts are (Your Gos, Your Chesses, Your Hives) but the level of strategy in this game is absolutely perfect for its short length. More importantly, though, the fact that its strategy is entirely centered around fierce player interaction just raises the fun factor above and beyond most abstracts for me. Lots of abstracts are competitive, but an abstract that plays well with 2-4 and is this cutthroat is a thing or rarity and beauty indeed. Blokus comes close, but there the mean plays come mostly in the endgame... whereas Hey, That's My Fish starts with is all teeth and claws (beaks and flippers?) from the very start, because there isn't time to fuck around.

Plus, adorable penguins! MEAN adorable penguins! THAT'S THE BEST KIND, YOU GUYS. Honestly I feel like the game's length + adorable factor wins over even my least-competitive friends. There's something that's just funny about the cute vs. evil dichotomy.

Update: This is the abstract that's gotten the most consistent play for me, so after many years with the original Mayfair version, I've upgraded to the FFG small box edition via a trade. Love it! Easy to transport, better & clearer art on the tiles, and the penguin minis are much cuter.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Hey! That's My Fish is one of the most deceptively ruthless games. On appearance, you have what appears to be a children's game with cute penguins and hex tiles of fish. And, the rules can be explained in about a minute, with a game lasting about 5 to 10 minutes.

Sounds silly and light? Just wait until you start moving your penguin pieces in this no-luck, chess-like, abstract game. Each player quickly begins to cut off one another, marginalizing each player and trying to capture the best areas. It is delightfully cutthroat, and I forget how good of a filler this really is. It's one of the best options for 5 minutes of gaming. 

For the record, I'm a fan of the deluxe edition plastic penguins.

RATING: 10
Pretty close to a perfect game. Kids love it for the theme and simplicity, but there is lots of room for strategy. A 2-player game between adults feels like a good game of chess. 

It's a perfect information game, which basically means that there are no hidden cards in your hand or the deck or any die rolls or anything random at all. Every bit of information you need to win the game is sitting right in front of you, and it's up to you to mess it up or not. 

My only complaint is how long it takes to set up versus how long it takes to play, and the fact that I constantly bump the other ice pieces out of place when I pick up the one my penguin is on. 

My wife described it as if a game of checkers decided to grow up and become a real game, but got taught by Phase 10. When played with adults, you end up loving the game and hating the players. 

At the 10-15$ price point, no one has any excuse not to own a copy.

RATING: 8.5
An AP-heavy game if you want to play optimally, but not doing so still makes the game super fun. This isn't a 'you always have 1 right decision' kind of game. You can use different strategies and still do well. It's super fun, super light, yet super heavy at the same time.

The mechanics here work better than any similar kind of game I've played. I have the tiny version of the game (the newest edition iirc). It works well at this size. If it were too big, it'd lose some of its value. It's a small and simple game, so having small tiles works perfect.

Set up is also quick. Just have all players help out and don't worry about optimizing the board layout - placing the penguins at the start is like Settlers - it's a self-balancing mechanism for the random board.

RATING: 7.5
This is an excellent game to start teaching the difference between short-term gains vs. long term goals. 

My tiny tably toppers love how they can say the phrase in so many different ways, to mean different things!

- Anger when someone beats them to a particular tile: [b]HEY!!![/b] That's my fish!
- Gloating when they got a key tile: Hey! That's [b]MYYYYYY[/b] fish!
- Confirmation that they just blocked you out of a huge section of ice: Hey! That's my [b]FIIISSSSHHHHH![/b]

If you can get the delux version - every kid loves penguin figurines. If you get the smaller version, go get one of those plastic toy guns that shoots "plunger stick bullets" (or whatever they are called). Then you can use the plunger to retrieve tiles that are hard to pick out from the middle.

RATING: 6
Extremely cute abstract game, but the theme veneer is charming and adds something to it for me. The game is basically all about positioning oneself and trying to isolate sections of the board if possible. The movement scheme feels something like Yinsh and Zertz combined, as you remove pieces from the board like Zertz, but have the movement range of Yinsh, and like that game the board piece that is effected is the one that you started the turn on.

I like the fact that the game seems to have plenty of range for good tactical play, but is still very quick to explain and very quick to play. Quite enjoyable, though its lightness and lack of depth mean that I wouldn't want to play it too often, because I imagine it would be an easy title to burn out on.

RATING: 6.5
I'm liking this one less than I did initially.  

The game begins with the climax; the first few moves often decide the winner, and the bulk of the game is essentially an extended epilogue.  Usually, you can stop playing several moves in advance, and determine the winner by simply tallying the remaining tiles.  

That's not such a bad thing.  In many ways, this forced, razor-edged decisiveness is preferable to a game that drags.  The whole experience is fast, exciting and painless.   I guess I just want a little more "epic-ness" in my abstracts.  This is more like a barroom brawl than a clash of powerful armies.  It's an interesting game, and I'll continue to play it, but my first impressions haven't quite held up, which is disappointing.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Components: Funky wooden penguins. Thick, attractive, functional tiles that are easy enough to handle. The box could be half as large.

Experience: The allure of the 3-fish tiles helps give the opening game some direction. As the penguins edge around each other, Go-style, the board's vulnerabilities begin to develop. Soon it's a tactical game of sectioning off chunks of tiles, with each player trying to ensure that their penguins will have uncontested access to fish when the endgame begins. Quick playing.

Other than the theme, this game could live happily among the GIPF series, as there are some pleasant similarities to TAMSK.

I've played enough now that I'm no longer itching to play, but each game is still absorbing.

First Played: 2006-09-26
Last Played: 2011-09-24
Eagerness to Play Again: Within a year

Plays (15):
2 players: 11
3 players: 3
4 players: 1

RATING: 7.7
I love the rules - very elegant.

Simple and easily explained within a couple of minutes but with loads of emergent tactics and strategies to employ.

As a 2P game, it's actually a deep abstract game but I imagine it as a fun, chaotic 3/4p.

2009-07-29 8>7.7

With 4p, it still feels fairly ordered - maybe because of the fewer number of penguins per folk, retaining some semblance of sanity in the game.

I feel that with multiple folk, it definitely becomes less strategic (as I expected) but rather than simply being chaotic and on the verge of 'too complicated to plan', it becomes beneficial to be competing with a weaker player (Finn giving John a large island she should have won).

I definitely enjoyed both the games, but it wasn't the riotous affair I expected. With the limited movement and power to only compete with those close to you, relative player strength of those you're competing with matters a lot.

RATING: 6
Players navigate their penguins over an 8 x 8 hexagonal tile game board.  As the penguin leaves a tile, it claims that tile as part of it's end of game score.  Penguins can't turn, jump over gaps or other penguins, thus get more and more restricted by the ever shrinking play area.  When all penguins are locked out, score the value of the tiles claimed (one to three fish each).  Highest wins.  Good game - seems to take longer to set up than play!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Hey, That's My Fish is typically thought of as a simple filler game, but there's actually quite a bit more going on than meets the eye. Aside from the random setup, the game functions as a no-luck area-enclosure game. Much more accessible and somewhat simpler than Amazons, the game is equal in play. The differing values on the fish tiles offer new players clear goals and create slightly different games each time.

Much hay has been made of the setup time. Honestly, I'm not sure that it's something you need to worry about. Yes, it takes a little while, but no more than a minute or two, and playing the game will take a good bit longer than that.

The game scales fairly well. Multiplayer abstracts aren't my favorite, but this one works well, avoiding excessive chaos while retaining interaction. There's an implicit lesson about fighting a two-front war that can be learned when attempting to save two penguins from threats from different opponents simultaneously. Recommended for a fan of abstracts, multiplayer or otherwise.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
This game is PURE EVIL! I was expecting a light kids' game. While this game could indeed be easily taught to children, there is actually a savage game of punch and counter-punch here. Collecting fish is secondary to screwing your opponents by leaving them stranded on ice flows, or strategically isolating yourself on large ice-flows with lots of fish. I like it. I especially like the fact that you can play a whole game in about 20 minutes. The components are nice. I suppose if I had one very minor gripe it's that setup can be a bit tedious, but that's a very minor point. The child friendly appearance makes me think of Reiner Knizia's Through The Desert. That game, like Hey! That's My Fish!, has colorful and kid friendly components, but it is actually a brutal and highly competitive game.

RATING: 7
[b][thread=476527]The PLAYMOBIL® Legion reviews "Hey! That's My Fish![/thread][/b]

(As of [b]9[/b] plays) A family-friendly game about penguins who mysteriously can't swim. The rules are extremely simple, but there is enough potential for strategic maneuvering to keep more experienced gamers interested. Set-up is a bit fiddly, but it plays fast (although can cause Analysis Paralysis in some - you know who you are, Eric) and seems to scale well from 2-4 players.

[b]2 year verdict:[/b] Still a fun game. Wouldn't mind playing more often (although with 2 players I would still prefer [GAMEID=2655].)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
For looking like a children’s game, Hey! That’s My Fish! is surprisingly cutthroat. New players will often spend their first few games making a beeline for the 3-fish tiles until they realize that the person who wins is the one who manages to isolate other penguins as soon as possible. Then the game becomes much more aggressive and tactical.

Hey! That’s My Fish! is certainly enjoyable to play. But there’s something about spatially-based games that doesn’t quite do it for me. I never get the sensation of digging my teeth into this game and chewing on it. If you can plan several moves ahead,  you should be able to set yourself up for a pretty good position in the endgame. 

And the endgame is where Hey! That’s My Fish stumbles a bit. Because you remove ice flows as your penguins move away from them, the game board gets smaller very quickly, thereby limiting your options and making it easier to see which move is best. The final few turns of the game consist of just moving your penguin around on its own isolated group of ice flows until you run out of room. The first three or four moves are the most critical; everything after that is merely a continuation of your original tactics. 

It’s a shame Hey! That’s My Fish! kind of sputters to a halt, because if the designers could have kept that same level of initial tension throughout, I would rank this as one of my favorite abstract games (along with Yinsh). But the ending is unfortunately anticlimactic. I’ll still happily play this game on occasion, but it doesn’t quite scratch my brain-burner itch.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
With 2 players, it's still an OK game, but it kind of feels like Chess then, the better player able to outthink his opponent most of the times. If after 5 plays the score is 4-1 or even 5-0, the other player wants to quit. Who can blame him/her ?

With 4 players, it becomes too much of a luckfest, as by the time it's your turn again, a lot of chaos has happened and you might be completely locked in.

So my feeling is this plays best with 3, as then some tactical skill is rewarded, but you still need a bit of luck as well. Only downfall is that you don't stand a chance at all if the others are playing against you. So if after a couple of games they sense you are the smartest, they will form a pact against you and you can forget about it. Hence my rather poor rating for this game. I like to compare it a bit to Tamega (coincidentally from the same year ?), but I prefer the latter, certainly with 2 players.

I also can't help but feel that this game is also missing something. More tiles and/or some special ones could do the trick.

RATING: 3
[Abstract Strategy] (Packeis am Pol) [2P:3, 3P:3] A simple idea that wasn't taken far enough as a game. Players plunk penguins down on a hex grid made of individual tiles. The players then move them around in straight lines. When a penguin leaves the tile it's standing on, the penguin's owner claims the tile. Shades of an even simpler, less random version of Verflixxt. Too short, and has all the depth of a children's wading pool, which is appropriate I guess since that probably is the extent of the target audience for the game. PS: If you like where the game was going, but are frustrated that it ended six stops short of its destination, check out Kris Burm's YINSH. It's got similar ideas but is executed differently, plus it takes the ball all the way into the end zone, complete with celebration. ***UPDATE: Still completely unremarkable, and has a tendency to be anticlimactic. I really don't understand the appeal beyond the fascination of some gamers with the penguin-shaped bits. Might be ok as a children's game. Think training wheels until the kid can graduate to YINSH.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Don't let this game fool you into thinking it's a kids game! It's a GREAT game for any age! Sure, your average 4 or 5yo can understand what they are doing, but the strategy is a bit deeper. When I really love it is when the kids leave the table and the gloves can come off.  About halfway through his first game (5 minutes?!), my 25yo nephew says, "Wow, this is vicious!".  And he's used to playing PR, so he's no newbie.

H!TMF has two of the three strategic elements of chess: timing and position.  The one that is missing is material; all pieces in this game have the same power. As a result, it is lighter, quicker, and more accessible.

See my full review at:
http://zwischen-zug.blogspot.com/2011/04/pocket-fishermen-hey-thats-my-fish.html

RATING: 6
Hey, that's my "it's a pain in the ass to set this up with all these Q!#$@# tiles considering how quickly this plays."

The FFG version is a feat of modern engineering in how they fit what was a Mayfair-sized game into a tiny little box.  The small tiles are kind of a bitch to handle though and makes the (relatively) lengthy set-up even worse.

Understand when I say "Relatively", I'm talking about in relation to the actual depth and length of gameplay.  It takes me ten minutes to set up War of the Ring; we'll play for three hours.  This takes me five minutes to set up; we'll play in about five minutes.  Grrrrrr.

Otherwise, a decent, but theme-light family abstract game that's okay, but it isn't going to blow my skirt up.  Cute artwork will make it appealing for kids.

For hvert træk bliver området man kæmper på mindre og et øjebliks uopmærksomhed kan betyder, at du er fanget på en isflage og isoleret fra den videre kamp om at samle flere af de eftertragtede fisk op, der er spillets point. RATING: 7
A fun game that can be picked up by anyone. It looks like a kids game but it's fun abstract strategy game to play. 
Players place their penguins in hexs and move around trying to collect fish, hexs have from 1 to 3 fish each, every time someone leaves an hex it will sink it and may cut paths to other hexs, if you're penguin is cut-off and doesn't have where to go it will also sink. At the end the player with most fish wins.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Similar to yinsh in that you can move a piece along a straight line as far as you want, as long as there are no other pieces blocking that path.
Similar to zertz in that the play area shrinks with every move made.
Similar to go, through the desert etc in that you get points for enclosing areas

Move your piece one or more steps along a straight line, holes or other pieces block your path. Take the tile that you started your move from. This tile will give you victory points at the end of the game.
The gameboard will quickly break up into smaller clusters, and you must position your pieces to get the best clusters for yourself. This often involves denying your opponents any good moves by blocking their pieces.
Some tiles have a larger point value, but in many cases it is better to get a big area of low scoring tiles for yourself than to fight over a few high scoring tiles.

The initial placement of pieces and the random board prevents standard openings and scripted play which makes the game feel relatively fresh every time.

Very easy rules make it possible to play with just about anyone. It takes no time at all to go through the rules, and the game is over in about 15 minutes which means many people will agree to at least try it once. 
This is an abstract strategy game, and the gateway suitability of this depends mostly on if you think your players find such games fun or not. But on the other hand, I have noticed that the cute(?) penguins makes the game a little bit less intimidating and some players are more willing to play this than other abstracts like zertz for example. 

I've seen many people complain about the ratio of setup time and play time. At 10-15 minutes play time, and 2-3 minutes setup time, it definitely is noticeable but I'm not bothered by it.

I like the 2 player version best since you have more control. The rating drops a point per extra player. The four player game, although more chaotic, is still fun, but mostly because it is such a quick game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Hey! That's My Fish is a thinky abstract game wrapped in a fun, family-friendly theme. The components (in the deluxe edition) are oustanding, comprising sturdy cardboard hexes and cute cartoonish penguin figures in four humorous postures. Setup takes a few minutes. The rules are simple and easy to remember. As a short, light-weight game, it is perfect for a prelude or postlude to longer, heavier games or can be played several times in succession.

In a two-player game, the competition can seem aggressive because a winning strategy often involves isolating and stranding opponent pieces. No luck is involved; therefore, if the two players are not evenly matched, the weaker player is unlikely to win. Turns can take some time while a thoughtful player decides how to optimize a move, but the other player can usually spend that time planning the next move.

This game might be appropriate for players with low vision. Color-blind players could play if the penguins are given distinguishing marks.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Penguins must have a good P.R. agent.  First they have a hit movie with March of the Penguins, and now a new game.  Hey! That’s My Fish! is a game with a cute theme of hungry penguins vying for their next meal.  

The rules are very easy with no ambiguities.  Play is swift:  20 minutes or so seems the usual time frame.  In spite of this, though, the game is quite tactical in nature, and there are numerous important decisions to be made throughout the short duration.  While gathering fish is most important, players must also play defensively in order to prevent opponents from cordoning territory from which they can reap the benefits without outside competition.  Additionally, it is useful to isolate opponents’ penguins so they may no longer move, or only have one or two more fish they can capture before running out of space.  Nasty, but hey -- to the bold goes the most fish!

Hey! That’s My Fish! is fun, fast and tactical, one of those perfect games for when time is short, or when you want to introduce folks to gaming.  The theme is non-threatening, and the rules can be explained in a minute or two.   Yet, the tactics and choices are significant, so skill prevails over randomness.  Plus, who could resist those adorable, smiling penguins?

RATING: 6.5
Sok a pingvin, de túl kevés a hal.
Maximum 4 pingvincsalád versenyez, ki is tud több halat összeszedni a jégmezőn. A gyors szabályismertetés után a rendelkezésedre álló pingvinjeiket a játékosok egymás után lehelyezik az előkészített jégmező (ennek előkészítése a játék leghosszabb feladata) egyik olyan lapkájára, amelyen csak 1 halacska van (van még olyan lapka is, amelyen 2 vagy 3 hal található, persze ezekből nagyságrendileg már kevesebb). Játékosszámtól függően 2-4 pingvint indíthatsz el a mezőn.
A körödben a 6 oldalú lapka 6 irányából az egyiken tudsz egy pingvineddel mozogni egy vagy több mezőt választásod szerint. Két dologra kell figyelned: se nem léphetsz át másik pingvinen, sem üres mezőn. Ahonnan elléptél, azt a lapkát megkapod és a rajta lévő halacskák száma adja a végén a pontszámodat.
Az értékesebb lapkákért komoly csaták folynak, de néha a nevető harmadik ügyes lépésekkel lezárja a viaskodók területét, lehetetlenné téve mozgásukat. Itt bizony egymás ellen tesznek a pingvinek, mert csak egyetlen család lakhat jól, illetve jobban a végén.
Könnyed játék, egyszerű szabályokkal, amelyekből kellemes játék kerekedik ki. A család kisebb tagjai részére is ideális szórakozás lehet.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This is a good 20-minute filler game.  It's easy to learn and play (even for younger kids), but could turn into an analysis-paralysis fest if you wanted to.  The 2-player game could seriously be compared to chess with penguins!  The main strategy is to block off other players so that you have a monopoly on a large section of ice floes which you can then pick up at your leisure.  However, I think that where you place your penguins initially is more critical to the outcome than any tactical moves during the game.  Also, if two (or more) players gang up on another player, that player is probably going to lose, which could invalidate the best-planned strategy.  In a 4-player game, you have only 2 penguins and so have little chance of planning far in advance.

So, I'd generally conclude that this is a random filler game; just enjoy it for what it is and don't think too hard about it. :)

RATING: 7
[Initial Impression: 7] 
This game is quite deep for such a quick, fun, and light-feeling game. It has the advantage of being incredibly intuitive and fast to teach, but allowing enough strategic flexibility in the intial positioning and responding to your opponents to make it worth returning to again and again. Even though it would play just as well as a pure abstract, the theme actually enhances the fun, as you can gloat as you grab fish that other players were clearly aiming for.  The strategy is all about positioning yourself to trap opponents on small ice floes, watching them float off to starve, while simultaneously trying to trap yourself on a large ice floe so that you can float off to get fat on a solo feast of fish.  Don't make the mistake of going for quick 3-fish tiles, since you can sometimes guarantee yourself a much larger score by taking a well-positioned 1-fish tile.  The four-player game feels as though it is spread too thin, as you only have 2 penguins to work with and more turns before you can act again - I wonder if getting a second set to make a larger board and using more penguins per player would revitalize the four-player game.  The two- and three-player games are both excellent, however. 

After more plays, I think I like this best as a two-player face-off, which really showcases the strategic opposition and the zero-sum nature of the game.  With 3 players (and also with 4), it actually requires a funny bit of cooperation between sets of players - Players A and B have to make sure C doesn't corner off a large section of the board, B and C have to work together against A, and A and C have to join forces against B.  This is all happening simultaneously and implicitly, and you obviously don't want to make a move that meets this coordinated aim at the expense of hurting yourself.  What this means is that the game can really suffer if one or more players fails to keep in mind this "semi-teaming" aspect of the game.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Great little game, takes longer to setup than play... increased rating to 9 with the delux edition

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Deceptively simple little game, that is accessible to family and friends, young and old. Under the amusing penguin theme, it is actually a profound abstract, much like multi-player Go or Othello--minutes to learn, a lifetime to master! The 3P is cutthroat with each player maneuvering three penguins; like Go, there are several 'battles' raging simultaneously, vying for territory, capturing valuable fish tiles, and cutting off opponents. Like Go or Shogi, tempo is key--the first one to move to the correct spot could prove devastating to others, but may result in giving up an opportunity elsewhere. The 4P is a tad more chaotic, as it is much more difficult to discern the optimum move, since it is always changing with every opponent's play! Quick, deep, and fun. The deluxe version with the 3D penguins rocks. Initial rating is an '8'.

Update (05/27/12) 20 plays: 3P is the sweet spot. With 3x penguins, each player has enough options to somewhat control the outcome. The outcome for 4P seems like a crapshoot. Two penguins is not enough. It is more of a game of "Chicken", to see who blinks first and cedes area to the other player(s).

Update (08/04/12) 25 plays: Yes, 4P is chaotic. It is strongly driven by what the other three players do collectively. A boneheaded move by one player can easily give the game to another, so the 4P is fragile, easily breakable. It is probably better to approach the 4P game as more family-level fun, rather than any meaningful mental exercise. Dropping to a '7'.

RATING: 7
Beautiful little strategy game for all ages.  Aim of the game is to move your penguins around a hex grid collecting fish, all the while the previously occupies tiles are being removed to create holes in the ice.

I love the fact you can block off your opponents and strand them on a small chunk of ice, and it's great fun trying to be the first to the most valuable tiles in the grid.  Highly recommended, particularly for families.

RATING: 5.5
My reliable gaming friend was dead on for this, too much set-up for the amount of return. Not only that but once set up the tiles are hard to pick up without disturbing the others. 

Now well these things can sometimes be overlooked in a game here they definitely detract as it is a light 10 minute game. The aspects I did like were the slight screwage factor of stranding an opponent and the 'no luck' factor but the game lacks in many other areas, scoring and strategy being big ones. 

Slightly overated in a TTR kind of way but would be an excellent game for kids and their low attention span or just a light light filler. 

Blokus Trigon and TTD kick all kinds of A__ on this one though.

El juego tiene una o dos reglas, creo recordar, la verdad es que es muy facilito.

Las partidas arrancan bien, intentando rodear a tus rivales para eliminarlos del juego, pero una vez que ocurre esto y los pingüinos quedan aislados, el juego es un ver pasar los turnos para que acabe sabiendo ya como va a quedar la partida.

La gracia del juego es tener a tus rivales cerca y cerrales los caminos, una vez pasado ese periodo el juego se acaba, aunque siga quedando partida.

Se trata de un juego táctico, en el que los movimientos adecuados son vitales, pero es un juego muy corto y no da para grandes cosas. El hecho de eliminar las losetas no permite que se pueda desarrollar una estrategia, pero tampoco que se alargue la partida.

RATING: 8
Such a good game. You think, "Oh look at the cute little penguins, it must be great for little kids."  But you're wrong.  This is one of the most selfish, cut-throat games you can play.  Every move you make screws over your opponents, and possibly yourself.  The board gets very small, very fast.  It's evil; pure evil.


If you can find it, get the older version with the larger tiles, which helps with set up time because the pieces don't feel so much like fiddly bits.  The larger tiles are easier for adults to manipulate and I believe makes set up much faster.

RATING: 7
Hey! That's My Fish! is a game I sometimes shudder to bring out because it looks so juvenile but it's a deep, cerebral game that in some ways plays like a multiplayer YINSH or Othello. It plays quick, is very easy to learn, and I haven't played it with a person that didn't like it. 

The largest problem with Hey! That's My Fish! is the setup time. The setup time is roughly half the time for each game - this has always felt very tedious. This remains a small point of contention but it is a fundamental component of any board game's experience, so anyone interested in buying it should consider it.

RATING: 6
First things first: the game only works with two. More than that and it becomes extremely chaotic and uncontrollable.

Now, if you do play with just two, it's a very solid tactical game which can be taught and finished in minutes. Components are lovely, and the more modern editions, which are quite small, can be easily carried around.

As long as games for two which can be finished in ten minutes or less, this is the best one I've played. The biggest issue it has is it's cumbersome to set up.

good filler :)
It is a whole different game with four than with two. With two it was actually quite light. With four however it became much more tense. With two play was quick. With four players there was sometimes some slowdown when a player thought too long about a move. But because the board changed all the time this wasn't much of a problem. The quality of the tiles are not comparable to the ones of carcasonne. But this isn't much of a problem. 
***Update*** After playing "Through the Desert rating drops. I still give it a 7 because it is a fun game. And the problem that a weaker player can decide the winner in one turn isn't here.
There is however another problem. That is that the endgame is an anti-climax. Because whole areas disappear from the board.  These secluded areas work much better in through the desert.

RATING: N/A
In Hey, That's My Fish!, players want to catch as many fish as possible with their waddle of penguins. Each turn, a player moves one penguin in a straight line over hex-shaped ice tiles with 1, 2 or 3 fish on them. The player then collects the hex from where the penguin started its movement from the table, thereby creating a gap which penguins can't cross on future turns. When a penguin can't move, it's removed from play with its owner claiming the tile on which it stands. The player who collects the most fish wins.

RATING: 4

RATING: 7.5
March of the Penguins vs Battle Royale.  While the theme blows a raspberry at all the seriousness in the world with greedy penguins that is only the tip of the iceberg.  Below the waterline is a deep tradition of abstract games. 

A simple move and remove mechanism, on a random board of hexagonal tiles, grabbing land while cutting down your opponents options is nothing new but it is given an invigorating twist by the scoring system (not every ice tile is the same with either one, two or three fish (points) on offer) which provide some interesting choices - there is the chance that the last penguin standing will not always be the winner.  Recommended for an abstract fan who wants to introduce their hobby to non-gamers in a irreverant way.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
While essentially this is an abstract family game, it makes sense thematically for the ice floes to disappear as you move the penguins move around, and that you can't change directions as you slide across the ice. The placing of the penguins to box in someone is important, and you need to balance getting the good tiles with not losing your penguins too early. At the same time, sometimes it is beneficial to cut off a section of the board so that only you have access to it. All in all, a nice easy filler that can be played strategically by gamers or chaotically for laughs by non gamers alike.

Cardboard thickness of the ice floes is good and there are 4 unique molds for the penguin models.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is an abstract with cute pieces (love the penguins!) and a light theme, and it's a good one. It only has a couple of rules, and those are easy to teach -- including to kids.

In our first play, my kiddo -- age 7 -- scored 37 points to my 43. Which is awesome! It's easy to pick up, and I can see strategies that will emerge over time.

It packs a lot into about 10 minutes, too. Not as much as, say, Hive, but it's not TRYING to be Hive, either. It's a light, fun abstract that's good for mixed age groups, which offers an enjoyable amount of depth.

---

So far, good with both 2 and 3 players.

Setup is a bit fussy, since the tiles are small and the "board" has no retaining elements. It's also pretty fiddly in play, since it's easy to mess up the whole array by bumping a tile...and you pick up a tile every turn.

Playing on a cloth surface would help.

---

Also good with four players. I continue to be surprised by how solid -- and nasty, in terms of hosing each other -- this game is.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7

Le plateau de jeu est composé de 60 tuiles "bloc de glaces" qui représentent la banquise. Chacun de ces morceaux de banquise contient de 1 à 3 poissons. Les joueurs vont pouvoir y placer leurs pingouins en espérant pouvoir s'empiffrer un maximum.

A son tour, un joueur peut déplacer un de ses pingouins horizontalement jusqu'à rencontrer un obstacle(un autre pingouin, la fin de la banquise). En partant, il récupère la tuile sur laquelle il était. Petit à petit, la banquise se réduit donc et de pauvres pingouins vont se retrouver isolé, tout juste bon à démarrer leur marche d'empereur, le ventre presque vide ! C'est triste la vie d'un pingouin !!!

Le jeu se termine quand plus aucun joueur ne peut déplacer un pingouin. Le vainqueur est celui qui possède le plus de poissons.

Hey! That's My Fish est la réédition d'un jeu sorti en 2003, de manière plutôt confidentiel, chez Bambus Spieleverlag sous le nom de Pingvinas.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Game in a Nutshell: Teams of Penguins move around a sheet of ice, breaking it up along the way, while trying to secure the most fish.

Played as: 2 (Yucata.de), 3 player (live)

Pros: It toes the line with simplicity and cute-factor for casual gamers and tactically intensity for more gamery gamers making it a excellent middle-ground for all types of people. Has a structured but organic flow to the game that appeals to me.

Cons: Maybe too simple at times as it can feel samey. It's possible for a player to eliminate themselves earlier in the game with a few bad moves. Likewise, the game can become very cut-throat and mean with blocking and similar tactics... which will be nice for some but also possibly hurt the feelings of others.

Other: If you really want to play up the cute factor, you can't go wrong with the deluxe edition which adds so much personality to the game. If you don't go deluxe, then you're still getting a game with solid mechanics.

Best Use: An introductory game that can grow to be a light brainburner.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Great. Should not be pigeonholed as a kids' game, although it does benefit from rules that can be explained in a minute. The long jumps add something to the tactical options. Best for two of course; viable for three but some room for double-teaming; a bit of a mess for four. 

As much as I enjoy HTMF, it's never going to get into that upper pantheon of abstract games for me, since once you decide on a goal (isolating a particular one of your opponents penguins, for example), there is usually one clear best way to accomplish that. I've seen long jumps used effectively, but the situations for that are relatively rare. There isn't much in the way of forks (even though it is good to play over lunch). So while I rate HTMF solely as a 2er (with more, it would go down), it stays safely below something like Twixt.

Please don't bother turning the tiles over or matching the exact array shown in the rules; just spread em out and play!

RATING: 8
https://boardgamegeek.com/geeklist/201593/item/4340830#item4340830

"The game plays fantastically at 2P, though initial placement can often have far-reaching impacts. At 3P and 4P, the board becomes very crowded, and there is a lot of 'ganging up on the leader' in play.

The theme is very lightly pasted on, but the game itself is strategic and cutthroat. One of my top 10 abstract games, if only the set-up were not so fiddly."

Like least - slightly fiddly setup each time.

[size=10][u][i][b]r{Initial Thoughts}r (after 5 plays):[/u][/b][/i][/size]
* A cutthroat affair masked by the most charming of themes
* Harming opponents >= working on one's own goals
* Scales excellently with the use of more or less penguins
* Good for fans of high player screwage, abstract fans (feels a bit like checkers)
* Initial rating: [b]7/10[/b]

[size=10][u][i][b]b{Further Thoughts}b (after 25 plays):[/u][/b][/i][/size]
* Discovered that this is an excellent introduction for young gamers as well
* Plays lightning fast with two players, and perfect for children's short attention spans
* Cutthroat play is a bit daunting to teach young gamers, but they catch on quick enough
* Further rating: [b]7/10[/b]

RATING: 7
My girlfriend, Dana, picked this game for us to play, because it has a silly title. It ended up being a super interesting game, and I'm glad she picked it.

Players move their penguins along ice, but as they move, the ice begins to disappear. Eventually, penguins can become trapped, which leads to much of the strategy of the game. How can I keep my penguins free and mobile, while forcing your penguins into a corner?

Hey, That's My Fish is quick and easy. More like quick and icy! lolololololol

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is my son's game (got it for Christmas '06).

The game is extremely straightforward; you set up a playing field of hexes with fish on them, place your penguins on the grid, and each turn you move your penguin and remove the hex that the penguin was last on.  Repeat until nobody can move any of their penguins, then count up the number of fish each person has acquired.

Light?  Oh, yes; it would float away if given the chance.  Fun?  Yes, it's light filler-type fun.  Is it the centerpiece of a gaming night?  Um, no; if you end up with this as the big game in a gaming session, then it was a light evening indeed.

Within it's sphere (light filler-type games), it works very well.  Don't try to make it any more than what it is, and the game is fine.  The rating reflects the reality of the game for what type of game it is and whether it fills that need, no more, no less.

RATING: 9
A very solid little filler game that sets up and play in 10-15 minutes. Excellent with kids and adults which is also a big positive. It feels like a bit of a cross between Trias and YINSH but the gameplay is different from those.

A very "efficient" design where the designer has gotten a lot of mileage out of a few bits and a mechanism.

This is essentially an abstract but the fun theme of penguins "fishing" on ice floes works well IMO.

Certainly a game worth owning and one of the very best fillers in my collection.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
An abstract game that features 60 tiles with 1, 2 or 3 fish on them. Each player has a number of penguins. After they move, the penguin eats the tile they are on, earning those number of fish as victory points. Movement is straight in any direction, but blocked by gaps in ice floe or other penguins.  It's a very cute, very simple game that plays quickly. I have played twice with four players, where it is slightly  chaotic, but I imagine the two or three player game can be quite strategic. Also, the first player has a slight advantage in being able to seed their penguins first and get the first move to capture fish.

RATING: 8
The game is deceptive.  The theme and layout pretend to be a child's game.  The reality, to me, is that this may be one of the deepest strategy/tactics games I own.  I may never forget the knowing look and laughter my Dad and I shared after one of my moves threatened to cut one half of the board off.  My Mom was clueless as I saw my Dad's understanding of the game change in his eyes.  My Mom played me later and did quite well, doing much better than she predicted.

Why this is not a 10:
-> I do not want to play this all the time
-> I enjoy this in little bits at a time.  The abstractness of it wears on me after a while - too many variables that really require more analysis time than I want to spend.
+ I will suggest it for sure and will not turn down a game

RATING: 9
Complementing the well-known shrinking board mechanism with the unequal tiles pretty much dismantles all strategies to conquer space from other similar games, and having the tiles put at random just keeps the interest every round of play. A good setup and a strategy are vital to succeed, but a single right choice at the right moment can be decisive as well.

So we're left with a very flexible game, accessible but intricate, entertaining straight from the first round, replayable and - what is best - it works wonders for any number of players involved.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Travestito da gioco per bambini è in realtà un ottimo gioco strategico di piazzamento. Simpatico e veloce è un gioco che consiglio, la possibilità di creare ad ogni partita un 'tabellone' differente lo rende longevo. Regole semplici, setup un po' noioso e lento. Esistono diverse versioni, quella italiana (Pinguin Pescatore) ha una scatola troppo grande rispetto al contenuto; vista l'indipendenza della lingua consiglio la versione inglese (Hey, That's My Fish!) oppure la versione Deluxe della Phanlanx, più grande ma con materiali migliori. Il gioco mi è piaciuto talmente che alla fine ne ho tre copie.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The simplest rules so often generate the best games, and there is no better indicator of this fact than here. This little penguin-shifting gem (totally abstract, to tell the truth, but actually gaining a little from its theme - a rarity in itself) is brain-burningly tough, but will be picked up by gamers and kids alike; the friendly theme will be inevitably warmed to. But there's a devilishly tough game of vector mathematics and double-guessing underneath. Beware!

Worth buying the deluxe version or some nice penguin figurines for the finishing touch.

Further Thoughts: Good, yes, but not 9-good. Downgraded to a more realistic 7.

RATING: 7
Was an instant hit with my family, but over time I couldn't get them to play it again, so I eventually sold it. But, to borrow from the old potato chip ad, betcha can't play just once. I like games like this, in which the rules are simple, but the strategy goes deep. It's rightly named one of the 'Top 20 games that adults love to play after the kids go to bed.' The penguin and fish theme is fitted over what's basically a thought-provoking abstract game. The only drawbacks are the set-up time to lay out all the tiles before being able to play, and the basically abstract nature of the game, but to me these are relatively minor points.

RATING: 8
A clever 15 minute opener for when you want a thinking game. The main idea is to head off your opponents and cut off islands of tiles that only you can get to and therefore score at your leisure, allowing you then to focus on moving your other penguins and claiming yet more tiles. With no luck in the game, it's all about thinking through moves and countermoves. Thumbs up.

RATING: 5
An abstract game with an engaging theme, in which your penguins collect fish that your penguin lands on. The aim is to create gaps which not only isolate a bounty but also limit your opponent penguin's movement. (This isolation element reminds me of Zertz, which I prefer because the player score status is simpler to determine so I get more competitive tension). Interesting as a spatial puzzle, I just can't get excited about it until I want to do the maths and think ahead about optimum moves. I'd imagine a good intro for kids who you want to push later into that horror called Chess.

RATING: 7
This is a fun filler game. In this game, players control penguin teams and the objective is to collect maximum fish even as the ice floes on which the penguins are break up.

A 4 player game doesn't take more than 20 minutes and where there is some strategy, there is a good dose of luck stemming from the initial configuration and the starting point where you place your penguins. The game offers a number of "grrr! I wanted that fish" moments justifying the name.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
Surprisingly deep given the cartoony art/theme and the overwhelming "this is a children's game" vibe that it gives off. It works at 2p, 3p, and 4p, and can be a bit aggressive when people try to cut one another off. Very confrontational and offers a not-overwhelming amount of lookahead for forward planning. Very quick to explain and takes a play or two to really start to grasp. Good candidate for the always-welcome "let's play again!" 

Nice risk/reward balance between doing a straight Fishgrab versus the more spatial claiming of territory, cutting people off, etc. 

This is my obligatory comment about the setup time: people complain about this as if it takes five minutes to set up and ten to play. It takes a little time to set up, yes, but complaints about the setup time are almost always hyperbole. It takes like 60-90 seconds.

RATING: 7
I enjoy playing this game with my children and my grandchildren.  The concept is simple, yet chess like.  You must think ahead.  First set up the tiles in a square.  Place your penguins (number of penguins dependant upon the number of players).  Players take turns moving their penguin one or more straight spaces picking up the tile the penguin was sitting on prior to movement.  The player with the most fish including the one you're penguin ends on wins

RATING: 7.5
Takes almost more time to set up than to play. Nice little game, perhaps a tad too strategic for newer gamers - I think people can kinda sense how the dryness of the game is covered up by the cutesy theme. Would like to see how this plays with kids.
As long as the players are of like abilities, than this game can play great.  VERY fast, and filled with decisions.
I would probably recommend it to more people as a good family game, except - it is ABSURDLY overpriced!
It is very surprising to me that a simple family-friendly game with some (boring wood) penguins and tiles, and it was priced at $25!
Then they figured that was too cheap (?!) and discontinued that version (which already was so high it turned off many prospective buyers, myself included) and then released the Deluxe version, with plastic penguins, and thought $40 was a pricepoint that people would accept for this kind of game.
And now it's out of print (?) - well, if you can pick up penguin figures somewhere (I'd suggest the Mumble Tumble version of Penguin Pile-Up, or just print out the little circles available here) and print out the tiles, you can try the game out and see if the original is worth that much $ to you.
(Own a print-and-play copy)

RATING: 7.9
Players: 2-4
Time: 15 min.

Light strategy game. The "board" is made up of hexagonal pieces of ice flow, with 1-3 fish on each piece. Players move their penguins on the board to claim fish, but each time, the last hexagon they were on is removed. As a result, the playing board disintegrates, and players must be careful not to let their penguins get cut-off from the "(sea-)lion's share" of the fish.

Great fun with kids.

RATING: 8
Played and bought at Essen 2007-10-18.  Very simple elegant pure strategy game with cute theme.  At first we forgot penguins can move more than one space, and it felt like the endgame of Fjordes, and seems fine as a variant!  Then playing it with full mobility made it like Yinsh or Terra Nova.  (I later learned it is similar to the game Amazons, studied by combinatorial game theorists.)  Quite good and plays very quickly.

There is a crazy persistent meme that "it takes as long to set up as to play", but this is nonsense. You're just dealing out rows of tiles! A single person can set it up in less than 2 minutes! (Literally; I've timed it.) If multiple players cooperate to deal out rows simultaneously, then it's even shorter. Anyone who "takes as long to set it up as to play it" is doing something wrong. (E.g. foolishly wasting time dealing the tiles out face down and then turning them all face up afterward, instead of simply dealing them out face up.)

RATING: 6
10-05-2015. Rated after 1 play. Fun abstract game, themed around pinguins collecting fish. 

Each turn, you move one of your X (depending on the number of players) pinguins to a tile. You have to move in a straight line though.. and you can't jump over water. Water you say? Every tile you leave, you take out of the grid and score the fish printed on the tile. If your pinguin ever can't move, it's out.

Fun, light, quick. Not much here, but what there is is good and interesting. I liked it a lot.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Perfect knowledge game, very abstract. But because pieces are removed as part of movement, this PK game gets easier to play as the game progresses. Good filler, cute pieces. Marginal set up time for a quick filler.

Penguins hop around ice floes and try to get the most fish. To play, you arrange 60 tiles into a random hexagonal grid, with each face up tile showing 1-3 fish on them. Players take turns placing their 2-4 penguins (depending on # of players), then players take turns moving one penguin. When a penguin moves, you pick up the piece that it started out on, and claim that # of fish. A movement is in a straight line, without jumping over gaps from removed pieces or any other penguins. The game ends when the ownership of the remaining tiles are no longer in contention. Add up your fish to see who's the winner. 

What tends to happen is players vie for the three-fish tiles, which immediately begins to fracture the board. The disappearing tiles create gaps and passageways, and this forces you to make some pretty good decisions for such a light game. Which penguin do I move? Should I block an opponent, or go hop on some big-fish tiles, or can I do both? If I try to fence off an area will I succeed, and will my resulting isolation be a benefit or a hindrance? Nice game. Plays very fast.

RATING: 6.5
Hey! That's My Fish! -- Played once; four-player.  This is really an abstract game.  The theme is established solely through the artwork.  The mechanics are entirely independent from the theme.  While the fun artwork brought some enjoyment to the play, I'm not sure that this wouldn't fare better without the superfluous theme.  In some games, the theme brings a coherence to the rules which makes learning the game easier or playing the game more fun.  In this case, the game gains no such coherence from its theme, so it can't lose any by eliminating the theme and simply using unadorned player tokens along with hexes depicting 1, 2, or 3 pips.  

For example, Ingenious (Einfach Genial) could have used a penguin theme -- Instead it was given handsome components, and it traded theme for style.  I believe Hey! That's My Fish! would do better to follow that model.  

I'm generally not a fan of abstracts, but because this can be learned so readily and it plays so quickly, I'll play it or not, as my group decides. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Playing this a bit more, rating's going up.

Playing more, it seems there is more to fish tiles (1,2 or 3 fish) than I'd like to care about, being more focused on areas, but maybe I'll wrap my mind around this. 

The game is simple to explain (for an abstract) and can be quite intuitive to play - I like the notion of moving along lines (not the chess type of moves by patterns)

Takes a while to set up, so get your group involved in it.

RATING: 8
The playing surface is 60 hexagons with one to three fish per hex. Move your penguins along a straight line without hopping over others and you take the tile your penguin started on. Continue until no one has legal moves remaining. Add up your fish, whoever has the most, wins. 

That's it. The box says 20 minutes, but unless you're playing HARD, your games should be over really fast. I would put this on par with For Sale as far as quick, light fillers go.

I would say Hey! That's My Fish almost has a YINSH feel to it because of the straight line movements. I like YINSH, but I love that i now have a 2-4 player abstract filler.

RATING: 8.5
Great, fun filler. Essentially an abstracted area-control game: players move penguins in straight lines across a tiled board and pick up the tile their penguin just vacated. Tiles are worth 1 to 3 VPs.

Once all penguins run out of moves, tiles are scored. Game plays quick, fast and there's lots of room for cutthroat play. It's all about not being caught in the corners and manouevring your penguins to section off a whole part of the board for yourself.

RATING: 8
It's really stunning how competitive and engaging this game is given it can be explained in two minutes. The players control between 2 and 4 penguins and move one of them each round, picking up the tile they moved from. This allows you to block your opponents and in that sense, the game reminds me of Through the Desert, except it scales better. Clever play is required to win the game but take your strategic thinking down a notch and it can also be enjoyed with kids. A solid entry that, at its price, should find space in everyone's collection.

RATING: 7
Very fun, multi-player, well-themed abstract.  It's a very quick game that takes place on an ice floe.  You move one of your three penguins any distance in a straight line.  You then remove the hex tile it was sitting on, claiming the # of fish represented on the hex (1-3).  Game over when no penguin can move.  My only complaint is that it seems to take almost as long to set up as to play.  Much quicker if two people set it up building out from a central line.  Highly recommended.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is a great abstract - Bruno Faidutti's game of the year, in fact! The board is a 7x8 grid of hexagonal pieces (floating ice tiles) with 1, 2, or 3 fish on them (randomly placed). Players get 2, 3, or 4 penguins (for 4, 3, or 2 player games, respectively) and take turns placing them on any 1-fish tiles, then take turns moving a single penguin. When a penguin moves, you take the tile it started on and add it to your score pile. Penguins may move for any distance in one direction to a new empty tile, but cannot jump over other penguins or empty spaces. The game ends when there are no legal moves left (you do get to score the final tile your penguins end up on). Scoring is simple: 1 point per fish. Highest score wins!

VARIANT: If one of your penguins is next to a penguin of another player and there is a hole in the ice in a straight line directly behind the opposing penguin, or that penguin is at the outside edge of the play area, you may move your penguin to that space and push the penguin into the water” (out of game). The ice floe you moved off of STAYS in play.

This is an abstract with a thinly pasted-on theme. But the theme works remarkably well! The pieces are cute, and the game plays very quickly. So despite my general dislike of abstracts, I do enjoy this one

RATING: 7
Fast, some AP, since it has quite a bit of "look ahead" involved, and fun.  Easy to learn and teach, plus it really does play in 15 minutes including set-up.  Also this can be played with fairly young players as they will get the mechanic quite easily.  Optimal play might come much later, but if you can 'self-limit' your own down-stream analysis, even young kids will make fun opponents.

Very strategic with 2 players, the player-added chaos will make the game much more tactical and faster as you add players.  Also for playing with kids playing with 3 or more players will flatten out the skill-curve and make the youngsters more competitive.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Of all the games I own, this is one of the fastest to learn (under 2 minutes), yet it has a shocking depth of strategy.  Despite the cutesy name and packaging, this is a game that can most definitely be enjoyed by adults as well as children (in fact, I think they should market an adult-oriented edition that includes a couple of well-chosen words between "My" and "Fish").  Once you realize that it is less about jumping on the 3-fish tiles than about trying to trap your opponent(s)'s penguins, then the game becomes almost Chess-like as you attempt to out-maneuver your opponents and react to their moves (my apologies to the venerable game of Chess for the comparison to the penguin game).  3 players seems to be the ideal number, although 2 works just fine.  With 4, I recommend playing as 2 teams of 2, with both players on a team combining their final score to see which team won.  I just keep wanting to come back to this game with all its simplicity, strategy, and fun.  It has rapidly become my favourite "filler" game, despite the unnecessarily-bitched-about need to spend a few minutes laying out all those hexes for the set-up.  So get over the name and the cartoony look already, and give this one a try!  Game design: 4.5/5  Personal enjoyment: 4.5/5  Total: 9/10

RATING: 6.5
[Phalanx 'Packeis am Pol' 2005 edition] {Abstract, animal; modular-board; scalable} Hey! That's my fish! is a nice family game.  It is also a very good game for children. The design is elegant!  It is easy to learn and teach.  Player interaction is strong.  Fun. No luck.  The game is so short that I won't be bored after a few games.  It's moderately deep and tactical but down time is not strong.  Recommended if you have children.

This is an excellent game for first-time designer.  Keep up the good work!

[House rule] When placing the initial Penguins, follow this order: the last player places first, then player places in anti-clockwise. After all players have placed the penguins, the start player moves first and follows clockwise. This makes the game more balanced, IMO.

RATING: 6.5

The set-up is very long for such a short game and can be a little boring if you're not the type for antics or you've only had a beer or two. But it is surprisingly strategic once you give it a chance. If I seem a little back-and-forth on this one, it's because I am; I think it's an "when the mood strikes" thing, but it's so cheap it was worth the purchase.

Suitability for Travel:

I have a 1 to 5 scale for four categories (1 is worst, 5 is best) in order of importance:

Portability (the less luggage space the better) - 4
Footprint (the less table space when playing the better) - 4
Scalability (the wider range of player counts the better) - 3
Learnability (the easier to teach non-gamers the better) - 5


Overall - 4

RATING: 9

It feels akin to Chess in that you have to think several moves ahead to do well and there are several different moves you can make each turn.  But unlike Chess, it is cute, goes up to 4 players, and plays extremely quickly.  The only slightly annoying part is the setup which takes unusually long for a game this small, but it isn't as bad as some people make it out to be, especially if everyone helps.  I am a big fan of this one.

RATING: 8.5
Stop complaining about the setup time.  It takes a couple of minutes at best - yes the game is short, but exactly how long does Agricola or Puerto Rico take?  Ticket to Ride?  Setup goes quicker if you don't worry about making a regular starting shape/board.  Just make a blob of tiles and go.  

Our 5 year old caught on to the blocking mechanism in just a few games.  A great game to introduce the kids to - you can tone down the agressiveness of your play for a few games until they get the knack. Great fun.

Seriously, don't be put off by the setup time complaints.

RATING: 9
This little gem of a filler has much more depth that it seems.  The theme is cutesy, but (like the ice flows you're hopping on)this abstract has about 80% of it's mass beneath the surface.  Its an area-control game with plenty of screwage opportunities where the constantly evolving (and shrinking) board keeps your head on a swivel.  Great game for all ages.

Rating of 8.5 based upon 2P game...which is where the tactical aspects of this game really shine.

A short (20 minutes) game in which players control a number of penguins. The penguins move over hex-shaped ice tiles with 1, 2 or 3 fish on them. The player takes the hex from where the penguin started his movement from the table, thereby creating a gap which other players can't cross. If a penguin can't move, he's taken from play. The player with the most fish in the end wins. Category: Animals, Abstract Strategy;  Mechanics: Point to Point Movement, Modular Board, Area Enclosure  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The game is very simple, but also just challenging enough for its time length.  It also can be played quickly, as a light filler, or more intensely, as you make an effort to plan your moves and trap other players.  It plays out differently based on the number of players in the game (with 2 players, you can save penguins to block certain areas; with 4 players, you don't have enough penguins to try that tactic), but that's not a bad thing.  I can see this being a big hit with families.

5 plays: 2 players
2 plays: 4 players

RATING: 6
This has a fair amount of meanness, for what is at first glance a very simple and abstract children's game. At least it seems like a kid's game when you factor in the silly premise and the cutesy penguins. It can deliver a pretty good brain burn if you let it, but there's not a ton of depth. As someone else around here mentioned, it sort of feels like the Tron motorcycle game; you have to watch your path to stay on the board, while at the same time try to cut your opponents off from their path. Once you have played it a few times, it becomes pretty repetitive, so I'm not sure I even like it as a filler...especially considering the set-up time is kind of a pain.

RATING: 7
2 - [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/tag/4p/user/Vroenis]4 players[/url].
Teaching: +2 minutes.
Mastery: 20 minutes.
Tiny box.
[url=http://boardgamegeek.com/geektag.php?tags=embassy_%26_outpost&username=Vroenis&action=usertags]Embassy_&_Outpost[/url]

[url=http://boardgamegeek.com/tag/outpost_mobile/user/Vroenis]Outpost mobile[/url].

[url=http://boardgamegeek.com/tag/semi-abstract/user/Vroenis]Semi-abstract[/url].
Movement.
Tile removal.
Enclosure/blocking.
Super light weight.
Medium player interaction.
Super light theme application (BGG lists it as abstract).

Move your penguin, take the tile it had just been standing on! That's it! Deceptively simple, but with a great potential for emergent strategy. A brilliant, simple gateway game or low mental-effort filler.

There probably isn't enough in this for long term veterans to keep visiting too often, but I suspect it'll be great to teach my nieces and nephew in a few years as a way to get them into contemporary games.

RATING: 9
"Like Chess and Go,  but I can understand what's going on"

The name is silly,  and I'm still on the fence about the wooden meeples...but this abstract/penguin game is pretty amazing game for a filler.  The only randomness is the board layout - the game itself has no randomness.  There are maybe a handful of rules,  and all of these can be explained in a couple minutes.  But there's plenty of nail-biting strategy,  and it plays easily from 2-4 players.

I would have used cute penguins like the "Don't Wake the Dragon" tuxedo penguins instead of meeple cutouts.  And it's definitely not enough for an entire game night...playing it a couple times in a row might be a bit much.  But you could easily pull it out again in a week - after all,  it's 15 minutes!  How many strategy games fit in a 15 minute slot?!

I have played once with the pushing variant - changes some moves,  but never actually got to see much pushing (you can usually see and avoid possible first-degree pushing situations)
