RATING: 7.5
This started off being one of my all-time favorites, mostly because of the theme (yay penguins!). I still like it a lot but have found overtime that I am not as good at it as I could be- I struggle a bit with the strategy component. Don't get me wrong though, I continue to enjoy it nonetheless. I like the variable board set-up, it really suits the game, and I like how fast it is to play. It is also really easy to learn and can be played without strategy too, which is sometimes successful. So overall, I feel that it is a strong game and I enjoy it a lot. It's just not as good a match for me as other games, now that I've been exposed to so many. I would rate it as a 7 for quality, but it gets a 7.5 since I enjoy it so much, despite how bad I am at playing.

RATING: 8.5
Don't let the theme fool you into thinking this is a game for children.  This is actually a remarkably strategic abstract game, cleverly hidden behind a theme that will get even non-gamers interested.  It can get downright cutthroat with skilled players.

Games seldom last more than 10 minutes so you can have numerous plays in a single sitting, and anyone that says it takes longer to set up than play is lying to you; if it takes you more than a minute to set up this game, you're doing something wrong.

RATING: 7
A must for parents of children 4 and up.  Have this in your home before a Chess set, Checkers set, or Snakes & Ladders set.  Difficult to imagine a better introduction to board games and abstract strategy.

o Perfect duration.

o Perfectly simple mechanics, and thus very easy to adapt rules and/or handicap for the very youngest. I've played it countless times with 5yo & 8yo; now introducing 2yo.

o The theme is irresistable and fertile for young imaginations.

For adults the game is pretty good, too, though with a board this small play tends to become trivial a few moves after initial placement.

Some reservations about the new and so-called "Deluxe" edition: considering that the original seems to have been discontinued, the "deluxe" tag fails to assuage it's 30% premium.  And I might add that's a pretty hefty surcharge for 16 mass-produced plastic figurines and nothing else whatever: no additional hexes for the adults; no new rule variations or scenarios. Dispite it's simple construction, the original kit probably justified purchase; at this point it's better just to assemble your own set of coasters and figurines from the toy box.

RATING: 8.5
Great, clever little game... I've enjoyed this immensely both online and face-to-face, with 2, 3 and 4 players. Scales very well, plays quickly, and deceptively nasty gameplay. The rules are very easy to teach, and it often takes only one play to see how everything works together. Plus, it's got penguins! Benefits greatly from a tight online interface at BSW - but even face to face, it's one of the better 15-20 minute strategy games out there.

RATING: 8
One of those games I quite like: rules that are easily explained, mechanics that allow (in principle) for very serious, concentrated tactical play, but that, probably because of the 'levity' of the game, aren't actually played that seriously most of the time, but lend themselves more to "casual & fun" (I'd say Abalone is another one of those, but only for two players).
Complexity of this one is a tad on the low side, but there are two big plus points: it can be played with more than 2 players (3 or 4 both work well), and the games are short, but not *too* short. Perfect in-between brain teasing game, or to play with friends and relatives who usually aren't into (board) games.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
When this game was originally released, it received very good ratings and even some great reviews explaining game play, etc.  After reading and researching this for a couple months, I decided to add this one to my growing collection.

I would like to point out that I think the components are VERY nice!  The 3-D penguins play into the theme better than the wooden figures and the tiles are nicely illustrated, durable, and easy to handle.

To be completely honest, the game play isn't very fun.  Setting up really takes a toll on players as the actual gameplay is only a fraction of the time it takes to set up the tiles.  This was disappointing and definitely annoying.  I am not a lazy gamer, but I found the setup (per instructions) to be such a downer!

When it comes to playing the game, sure it is fun... for the first few rounds.  Then, everything becomes VERY redundant and dull.  

Children will a blast playing this game and I would highly recommend it.  As far as adults go, your money would be better spent on something else.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I'd mentioned it to my son in passing and he actually asked for it for Christmas .. an opportunity I wasn't going to miss.

This is about as simple as it gets but can be great fun. My son doesn't like much confrontation but with this he really gets into the fun of it. Its so quick to play that its not really a huge deal when someone deliberatly cuts off your penguins from the best fish. Its so obviously a valid tactic that everyone does it and theres never any hard feelings.

The only down side, and I'm clutching at straws, is that it can take longer to lay out the tiles than to play! For that reason alone we'll limit ourselves to maybe 3 games in a sitting so it doesn't get tedious but its a fantastic intro game to get everyone into a competative and fun frame of mind.

Skilled players will win. My dad, in his first 3 games, wupped us mercilessly. But he's played a lot of chess and draughts and is good at seeing patterns and planning his own and other moves well in advance.
